            .mktoForm .mktoFormRow ._6si_sff_filled {
                display: none;
            }
            .hs-form .hs-form-field:has(._6si_sff_filled) {
                display: none;
            }
            .hs-form .hs-form-field ._6si_sff_filled {
                display: none;
            }
            form.form .form-field:not(.error):has(._6si_sff_filled) {
                display: none;
            }
            form.form .form-field:not(.error) ._6si_sff_filled {
                display: none;
            }
            .elq-form .row:has(._6si_sff_filled) {
                display: none;
            }
            .elq-form .row ._6si_sff_filled {
                display: none;
            }
            .elq-form .field-wrapper:has(._6si_sff_filled) {
                display: none;
            }
            .elq-form .field-wrapper ._6si_sff_filled {
                display: none;

data-stepid="SH2SYIVKSBSG8YO"><h2 class="step-title">Step 2: How It Works?</h2><div class="mediaset"><div class="photoset-wrapper">
    <div class="photoset"><div class="photoset-row items-3 "><div class="photoset-item photoset-cell" style="-webkit-flex: 1.5; flex: 1.5;" data-imagenotes="[]">
    <div class="photoset-image">
        
            <a class="gallery-link" rel="photoset79" href="https://content.instructables.com/FO8/QWAQ/KSBSG8YJ/FO8QWAQKSBSG8YJ.jpg?auto=webp&amp;frame=1&amp;width=1024&amp;height=1024&amp;fit=bounds&amp;md=eaa0b1335f46e3329446c14667d22190" data-download="https://content.instructables.com/FO8/QWAQ/KSBSG8YJ/FO8QWAQKSBSG8YJ.jpg?auto=webp&amp;frame=1&amp;md=eaa0b1335f46e3329446c14667d22190" data-fileid="FO8QWAQKSBSG8YJ">
                <img loading="lazy" alt="How It Works?" src="./código_files/FO8QWAQKSBSG8YJ.jpg">
                
            </a>
        
    </div>
</div><div class="photoset-col" style="-webkit-flex:0.75;flex:0.75;"><div class="photoset-item photoset-cell" style="-webkit-flex: 1.5; flex: 1.5;" data-imagenotes="[]">
    <div class="photoset-image">
        
            <a class="gallery-link" rel="photoset79" href="https://content.instructables.com/F6Q/DXGN/KSBSG930/F6QDXGNKSBSG930.jpg?auto=webp&amp;frame=1&amp;width=1024&amp;height=1024&amp;fit=bounds&amp;md=3af0b2f8ff0db581b377915b97630162" data-download="https://content.instructables.com/F6Q/DXGN/KSBSG930/F6QDXGNKSBSG930.jpg?auto=webp&amp;frame=1&amp;md=3af0b2f8ff0db581b377915b97630162" data-fileid="F6QDXGNKSBSG930">
                <img loading="lazy" alt="How It Works?" src="./código_files/F6QDXGNKSBSG930.jpg">
                
            </a>
        
    </div>
</div><div class="photoset-item photoset-cell" style="-webkit-flex: 1.5; flex: 1.5;" data-imagenotes="[]">
    <div class="photoset-image">
        
            <a class="gallery-link" rel="photoset79" href="https://content.instructables.com/FU4/YJJ3/KSD7W1TP/FU4YJJ3KSD7W1TP.png?auto=webp&amp;frame=1&amp;fit=bounds&amp;md=51a2ba6c79993b465aafcbe2a1eadb18" data-download="https://content.instructables.com/FU4/YJJ3/KSD7W1TP/FU4YJJ3KSD7W1TP.png?auto=webp&amp;frame=1&amp;md=51a2ba6c79993b465aafcbe2a1eadb18" data-fileid="FU4YJJ3KSD7W1TP">
                <img loading="lazy" alt="How It Works?" src="./código_files/FU4YJJ3KSD7W1TP.png">
                
            </a>
        
    </div>
</div></div></div></div>
</div></div><noscript><div class="no-js-photoset"><img loading="lazy" alt="How It Works?" src="https://content.instructables.com/FO8/QWAQ/KSBSG8YJ/FO8QWAQKSBSG8YJ.jpg?auto=webp&amp;fit=bounds&amp;frame=1&amp;height=1024&amp;width=1024auto=webp&amp;frame=1&amp;height=300"><img loading="lazy" alt="How It Works?" src="https://content.instructables.com/F6Q/DXGN/KSBSG930/F6QDXGNKSBSG930.jpg?auto=webp&amp;fit=bounds&amp;frame=1&amp;height=1024&amp;width=1024auto=webp&amp;frame=1&amp;height=300"><img loading="lazy" alt="How It Works?" src="https://content.instructables.com/FU4/YJJ3/KSD7W1TP/FU4YJJ3KSD7W1TP.png?auto=webp&amp;fit=bounds&amp;frame=1auto=webp&amp;frame=1&amp;height=300"></div></noscript><div class="step-body"><p style="text-align: justify;">The working of this project is based on an Infra Red Sensor, This sensor is the heart of this project. </p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>Let's take a look to the IR Sensor.</em></strong> In picture I shown a typical IR Sensor, basically it has a transmitter IR LED, A photo Diode, an Opp-amplifier IC and a potentiometer. </p><p style="text-align: justify;">The photo diode is placed just next to the IR LED in such a way that it can not receive IR rays directly. Photodiode is sensitive to the IR radiation. It's cathode connected to the positive voltage i.e. 5volt and anode connected to the noninverting input of the Opp-amplifier which also get pulled down though the 10Kilo ohm resistor. Potentiometer in IR sensor is use to set the sensitivity distance of the sensor, it connected to the inverting input of the Opp-amplifier.  IR LED continuously transmit the infra red rays and if any object comes in front of it, IR rays get reflected back and it received by the photo diode due to this change in IR radiation the voltage at the anode get change, the change in anode voltage is depend on the IR radiation received by the photo diode. More the IR radiation received grater will be the change in anode voltage. The output of the IR Sensor taken from the output of the Opp-amplifier. We can adjust the sensitivity distance by rotating the potentiometer on the sensor, we rotate the potentiometer that means we set a threshold voltage for the noninverting input of the Opp-amplifier. Whenever the voltage on the noninverting input is greater than the threshold voltage, the voltage on the noninverting input i.e. +ve voltage from the photodiode get forwarded and get the positive pulse at the output of the Opp-amplifier i.e. output of the sensor.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><em>A typical IR sensors circuit diagram is attached check it for reference.</em></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><b style="font-style: italic;">Let's see the main circuit diagram of the project. </b>I connected a IR sensor to the Arduino Pro Mini board as Vcc of the sensor to the vcc of the Arduino Pro Mini, Ground to the ground and the output of the sensor to the Analog pin one (<strong>A1</strong>) of the Arduino Pro Mini. I used a 5 volt buzzer and a vibrator motor from the old cellphone for alerting. I connected both buzzer and vibrator motor in parallel and used an general purpose NPN Transistor (<strong>BC547</strong>) to drive them. Transistor's emitter connected to the ground and collector connected to the negative pin of the buzzer and vibrator motor. Positive terminal of vibrator motor and buzzer are further connected to the vcc of the Arduino Pro Mini. Base of the transistor connected to the pin D3 of the Arduino Pro Mini through the 4.7 kilo ohm resistor.        </p></div></section><section id="step3" class="step" data-stepid="SK7KC79KSD7W31H"><h2 class="step-title">Step 3: </h2><div class="mediaset"><div class="photoset-wrapper">

I stick the sensor over the Arduino pro mini board using hot glue and solder it with short flexible wires. After next to it, I made a buzzer unit, in which the vibrator, buzzer and transistor is include, which I mount on left stick of glasses near ear. Also stick the battery on the same stick and mount an on off button near to the left eye. stick the sensor to the frame such as it will close to eye. the distance between the eye and the sensor will not more than 15 to 20mm . </p></div></section><section id="step4" class="step" data-stepid="SY4PIVGKSD7W77X"><h2 class="step-title">Step 4: </h2><div class="mediaset"><div class="photoset-wrapper">
    <div class="photoset"><div class="photoset-row items-3 "><div class="photoset-item photoset-cell" style="-webkit-flex: 1.5; flex: 1.5;" data-imagenotes="[]">

Now let's understand some settings and programming.  </p></div></section><section id="step5" class="step" data-stepid="SLAXC54KSD7W5PW"><h2 class="step-title">Step 5: Sensor Setting</h2><div class="mediaset"><div class="photoset-wrapper">
    <div class="photoset" style="max-width: 1050px;"><div class="photoset-row items-1 "><div class="photoset-item photoset-cell" style="-webkit-flex: 1.5; flex: 1.5;" data-imagenotes="[]">

    </div>

</div></div><noscript><div class="no-js-photoset"><img loading="lazy" alt="Sensor Setting" src="https://content.instructables.com/FA6/293D/KSBSG2T0/FA6293DKSBSG2T0.png?auto=webp&amp;fit=bounds&amp;frame=1&amp;height=1024&amp;width=1024auto=webp&amp;frame=1&amp;height=300"></div></noscript><div class="step-body"><p style="text-align: justify;">It will be better if you do this before sticking the sensor on the frame, After connecting all the components power up it. Now set the the sensors sensitivity distance to minimum. About 10 mm or less..</p></div></section><section id="step6" class="step" data-stepid="SYX901HKSD7W8KN"><h2 class="step-title">Step 6: Programming.</h2><div class="mediaset"><div class="photoset-wrapper">
    <div class="photoset"><div class="photoset-row items-4 "><div class="photoset-item photoset-cell" style="-webkit-flex: 1.5; flex: 1.5;" data-imagenotes="[]">
    <div class="photoset-image">
        
            <a class="gallery-link" rel="photoset104" href="https://content.instructables.com/FPZ/1U89/KSBSG2TP/FPZ1U89KSBSG2TP.png?auto=webp&amp;frame=1&amp;width=1024&amp;height=1024&amp;fit=bounds&amp;md=95f062cc4119740a0f7c146df1e3a590" data-download="https://content.instructables.com/FPZ/1U89/KSBSG2TP/FPZ1U89KSBSG2TP.png?auto=webp&amp;frame=1&amp;md=95f062cc4119740a0f7c146df1e3a590" data-fileid="FPZ1U89KSBSG2TP">

    </div>
</div><div class="photoset-col" style="-webkit-flex:0.5;flex:0.5;"><div class="photoset-item photoset-cell" style="-webkit-flex: 1.5; flex: 1.5;" data-imagenotes="[]">
    <div class="photoset-image">
        
            <a class="gallery-link" rel="photoset104" href="https://content.instructables.com/FPB/V7TV/KSBSG2TN/FPBV7TVKSBSG2TN.png?auto=webp&amp;frame=1&amp;width=1024&amp;height=1024&amp;fit=bounds&amp;md=ceb6205b82944a695fe2223cd589f48c" data-download="https://content.instructables.com/FPB/V7TV/KSBSG2TN/FPBV7TVKSBSG2TN.png?auto=webp&amp;frame=1&amp;md=ceb6205b82944a695fe2223cd589f48c" data-fileid="FPBV7TVKSBSG2TN">

    <div class="photoset-image">
        
            <a class="gallery-link" rel="photoset104" href="https://content.instructables.com/F0Q/FYCO/KSD7W8VV/F0QFYCOKSD7W8VV.jpg?auto=webp&amp;frame=1&amp;width=1024&amp;height=1024&amp;fit=bounds&amp;md=a8c2db99fd7b78b80466b08cde3695e2" data-download="https://content.instructables.com/F0Q/FYCO/KSD7W8VV/F0QFYCOKSD7W8VV.jpg?auto=webp&amp;frame=1&amp;md=a8c2db99fd7b78b80466b08cde3695e2" data-fileid="F0QFYCOKSD7W8VV">

            </a>
        
    </div>

    <div class="photoset-image">
        
            <a class="gallery-link" rel="photoset104" href="https://content.instructables.com/FYL/7IJN/KSBSG2TO/FYL7IJNKSBSG2TO.png?auto=webp&amp;frame=1&amp;width=1024&amp;height=1024&amp;fit=bounds&amp;md=c3c36d4460ba5ec76b9077b36ed48837" data-download="https://content.instructables.com/FYL/7IJN/KSBSG2TO/FYL7IJNKSBSG2TO.png?auto=webp&amp;frame=1&amp;md=c3c36d4460ba5ec76b9077b36ed48837" data-fileid="FYL7IJNKSBSG2TO">
                <img loading="lazy" alt="Programming." src="./código_files/FYL7IJNKSBSG2TO.png">
                
            </a>
        
    </div>
</div></div></div></div>
</div></div><noscript><div class="no-js-photoset"><img loading="lazy" alt="Programming." src="https://content.instructables.com/FPZ/1U89/KSBSG2TP/FPZ1U89KSBSG2TP.png?auto=webp&amp;fit=bounds&amp;frame=1&amp;height=1024&amp;width=1024auto=webp&amp;frame=1&amp;height=300"><img loading="lazy" alt="Programming." src="https://content.instructables.com/FPB/V7TV/KSBSG2TN/FPBV7TVKSBSG2TN.png?auto=webp&amp;fit=bounds&amp;frame=1&amp;height=1024&amp;width=1024auto=webp&amp;frame=1&amp;height=300"><img loading="lazy" alt="Programming." src="https://content.instructables.com/F0Q/FYCO/KSD7W8VV/F0QFYCOKSD7W8VV.jpg?auto=webp&amp;fit=bounds&amp;frame=1&amp;height=1024&amp;width=1024auto=webp&amp;frame=1&amp;height=300"><img loading="lazy" alt="Programming." src="https://content.instructables.com/FYL/7IJN/KSBSG2TO/FYL7IJNKSBSG2TO.png?auto=webp&amp;fit=bounds&amp;frame=1&amp;height=1024&amp;width=1024auto=webp&amp;frame=1&amp;height=300"></div></noscript><div class="step-body"><p style="text-align: justify;">Arduino pro mini dose not comes with any type of USB connector for programming, that's why it's hard for beginner to program it. But don't worry here I describing an easy way for uploading the program to Arduino pro mini. Take an arduino uno and remove its main IC i.e. AtMEGA328P. and then wire up it with arduino pro mini as shown in the above picture.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">          Arduino UNO                           Arduino Pro Mini </p><p style="text-align: justify;">                 Vcc -------------------------------- Vcc </p><p style="text-align: justify;">                 GND ------------------------------ GND </p><p style="text-align: justify;">                  Rx --------------------------------- Rx </p><p style="text-align: justify;">                  Tx ---------------------------------- Tx </p><p style="text-align: justify;">                  Rst --------------------------------- Rst </p><p style="text-align: justify;">After wiring connect Arduino Uno with computer using USB cable. Copy the following Arduino code and pest it in Arduino ide. Now goto tool menu and select board Arduino Pro mini, Again goto tool menu and select COM port. And Now click on upload Button. after uploading the program all done and its ready to play.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>Let's Understand the code</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><em>The code is very simple, it's just for managing the delay for activating the buzzer after the sensor input </em></p><pre>&lt;p&gt;int Sinput = A1;    // creating or assigning an int type variable for sensor input signal&lt;br&gt;int Buz=3;            // creating or assigning an int type variable for output buzz and vibrator&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;void setup()      /// in void setup we make the selected pins output or input.
{
  
&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;pinMode(Sinput, INPUT);  /// here it is sensors pin  so we are defining here that this pin is input pin 
pinMode(Buz, OUTPUT); /// here it is the pin used for transistor to control it,   so we are defining here that this pin is output pin&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;}
void loop()  
{
 
   
    if(digitalRead(Sinput)==LOW)
     {
       delay (2000);    // we are waiting for two second after the input pulse from the sensor. if the pulse is for more than  2 second then buzzer get triggered
  
       digitalWrite(Buz, HIGH);
     }
     else
      {
   
        if(digitalRead(Sinput)== HIGH)
            {
              
               digitalWrite(Buz, LOW);
           }
 
      }
   }&lt;/p&gt;</pre></div></section><section id="step7" class="step" data-stepid="SW12UV3KSD7WMWU"><h2 class="step-title">Step 7: </h2><div class="mediaset"><div class="photoset-wrapper">
